It is learned that the initial joint suppression by the Fujian and Guangdong armies is to first annihilate the communists in Zhao'an.

Overview of the World's Five Strongest Economies Last Year 74

— Translation should be done.

England

The economic situation in England in 1935 showed a significant improvement compared to the previous year. However, many industrial sectors were still far from reaching the levels of 1929 (before the economic crisis). There were anxieties in many areas of the economic world regarding the prospects for the future, especially from the perspective of the international situation. The influential Midland Bank published a monthly report stating that the world situation was creating a bad atmosphere, which would hinder future economic improvement.

Official figures released by the Department of Commerce showed an increase in foreign trade and shipping. Steel production had made significant progress, which corresponded to the demands of the heavy industry protected by high tariffs over the past three years for major transformations, and also met the needs of the war industry.

On the other hand, coal exports fell between July and September last year compared to the same period in 1934, and in October fell from 3,630,000 tons (1934) to 3,290,000 tons (1935). According to the newly published "Economist", exports of manufactured goods and railway freight fell sharply in November, partly due to sanctions against Italy. The electricity consumption index, which has always been regarded as a barometer of the UK's industrial prosperity, showed a decline in the last few months of last year. The index for October 1934 was 103.1, but in October 1935 it fell to 90.5.

At the end of last year, workers in many industrial sectors in the UK demanded wage increases, most notably in the mining and textile industries. In the first eleven months, there were a total of 551 labor disputes in industry last year, an increase of about a quarter compared to 442 in 1934, while the number of workers involved in these conflicts increased from 119,000 to 267,000, more than doubling.

United States

In 1935, the total industrial production in the United States increased by 10%, but it was still 30% below the level of 1929. According to official figures, the total agricultural income in 1935 was only 7.8 billion US dollars, which was far from the 11 billion US dollars in 1929.

Many daily newspapers and magazines stated that the economic improvement was not stable, and that new disputes might occur in 1936, affecting all important sectors of industry. For example, the December issue of the National City Bank Bulletin stated that the United States was facing some unfavorable economic factors, and that industry and commerce in 1936 might fall into stagnation.

The unemployment figures in the United States are still very high. According to various surveys, there are at least 11 million, and according to the Hamilton Society's calculations, there are as many as 13 million. Wages have remained at previous low levels, while food prices and rents have increased by almost 10% in 1935.

According to official figures released in 1935, although the government subsidized farmers to reduce cultivated land, 1935 was a year of deepening poverty for most farmers. In every thousand households, twenty-one had their properties auctioned off for debt, and more than seven had their properties auctioned off for unpaid taxes. According to statistics, 300,000 tenant farmers in the southern states had no land to cultivate due to the reduction of cotton fields.

Germany

Frenzied war preparation and severe food shortages—these two points are most noteworthy when examining Germany's economic position in 1935.

The war industry has developed greatly, but the production of consumer goods manufacturing industry has declined.

The status of agriculture does not seem to have improved much. Although grain production was higher than in 1934, it was still lower than the average annual production of the past five years. The harvest of sweet potatoes fell from 46.7 million tons in 1934 to 39.5 million tons in 1935.

The livestock industry has been hit hard. Originally, Germany's foreign exchange reserves were largely used for the import of raw materials for the war industry, so the import of feed was inevitably reduced.

Germany faced a painful financial situation in 1936. The national debt has accumulated to more than 40 billion marks. The Minister of Finance has publicly announced that in order to meet the needs of the war budget, it is necessary to collect the "last copper coin" from the people.

In terms of foreign trade, last year was also an unfortunate year for Fascist Germany. Although export trade was relatively stable compared to 1934 (based on the index from January to October), import trade was greatly reduced.

German fascist newspapers also inevitably revealed the fact that the cost of living has increased greatly. Advertisements in large stores indicated that prices had increased by 40% to 60% in one year.

Unemployment has increased dramatically. Even the Fascist newspapers, whose calculations should be discounted, published unemployment figures of nearly two million. In fact, the number of unemployed people is far greater than that number.

The most obvious manifestation of the poverty of the German masses is the high rise in the mortality rate. The mortality rate in 1934 was 10.9 per thousand, while in 1935 it reached 13.7 per thousand. In several large cities, there was a record of 2,715 suicides in three months. In Berlin alone, five or six people commit suicide every day.

In addition to suicide, many people also died for political reasons. Since the Nazi Party came to power, a total of 48,701 anti-fascists have been killed. There were a total of 5,425 anti-fascist cases. 21,000 people were sentenced to a total of 39,792 years in prison. If the prison terms of all political prisoners in concentration camps are added, it will total about 100,000 years.

Italy

At the end of last year, Italy was in a very tense atmosphere as a result of the war against Abyssinia. Italy encountered great difficulties both on the military front and at home, which even its own newspapers did not want to hide.

Italy went through many years of bad luck, carried out the war against Abyssinia, and the implementation of international sanctions closed many markets to Italian exports, so the economic crisis was of course even more serious. In order to meet the needs of the war, the industry was reorganized, and as a result, the production of heavy industry has increased greatly in recent months. In July 1934, the machinery construction index exceeded the level of 1929 by 5% and the level of 1934 by 36%. The production of the automobile industry increased by 25% compared to the figures in 1929. Steel production has also increased significantly. In the first seven months of 1935, the total iron production was 336,000 tons, while in the same period in 1934 it was only 299,000 tons, and steel production also increased in the same period.

During the same period, despite the amazing increase in the production of those industrial sectors that adapted to military needs, the industrial production index fell significantly in the summer months of 1935. In July 1935, it decreased by 15% compared to 1929 and by 20% compared to May 1925.

This decline was due to the great decline of the manufacturing industry. The textile industry was particularly hit hard. In July 1935, the silk industry index was only 9.5, while in July 1934 it was 50.6 (taking 1929 as 100%). The agriculture, which was greatly affected by the sanctions, also had the same situation. More than half of Italy's exported fruits could not be shipped to the countries that imposed sanctions. Wine exports decreased by a quarter. The war forced the Italian government to use all the available currency and gold reserves, which has had a profound impact on finance.

Japan

In 1935, Japan's national economy as a whole became more concentrated to meet the needs of the so-called "emergency"—or the preparation for "great war". Therefore, the budget for 1936-37 was again a purely military budget. Among the total national expenditure of 2.27 billion yen, more than half was spent by the Army and Navy, along with nine other items related to war needs. At the same time, the funds allocated to agriculture, which was considered to be in a critical situation, were further reduced.

Therefore, in 1935, Japan's industry showed a remarkable one-sided prosperity. Those industries that supplied military needs made progress, while other industrial sectors, especially those that supplied consumer goods, lagged far behind.

Japan is now facing a severe financial difficulty. The unsold government bonds held by the Bank of Japan amounted to a huge amount of 320 million yen. This led to the largest inflation since 1927. Compared with 1.763 billion yen at the end of 1934, the total amount of banknotes in circulation now exceeds 2 billion yen.

Accompanying this so-called "one-sided prosperity" of Japan is the gradual decline in the living standards of workers and farmers. Wages are gradually falling, while the cost of living is rising. Taking the wage index in 1934 as 100, the index in October 1935 was 81, lower than 82.6 in October 1934. At the same time, taking the retail price index in 1934 as 100, December 1935 was 155.6, while December 1934 was 150. These are just average figures. In fact, the prices of goods consumed by the masses have risen even more sharply. For example, the price index for food rose from 150 in December 1934 to 233 in December of the previous year, while clothing rose from 149 to 183.

Page 10

Bandit Yu Dingren, Zhang Changshui, and others formed a gang. These bandits roamed and harassed the border areas of Fujian and Guangdong without a fixed location. Now that the government troops are about to launch a large-scale campaign to suppress them, the bandits know that it will be difficult to resist and are likely to collapse towards the Yunxiao area. They had a fierce encounter with the Fujian and Guangdong troops a few days ago, resulting in more than ten bandits being killed and more than ten rifles being seized. In addition, when Guangdong Province handled the rural pacification a few years ago, the Communist bandits who gathered in Raoping were driven into the Zhao'an County area. The bandit leader was Wu Jin, a native of Qiongzhou. In July of last year, under the order of the pseudo-Southwest Fujian Military Region, he sneaked into the sixth district of the county and incorporated the bandit gangs of Yu Dingren, Yu Qitou, and Yu Hongmao. He called himself the Political Commissar of the Zhao Yunlong Red Army Command. Now, the various bandit gangs have been reorganized into the Zhao'an Battalion, Pinghe Battalion, and Yunxiao Battalion, and a pseudo-command post has been set up in Pingshui Camp, engaging in robbery and looting every day. Among the bandits, Yu Qitou is the most fierce and has resisted the government troops several times. At present, the men in the villages occupied by the bandits have been organized into the Red Guards, and the women have been organized into the porter teams. When the bandits first came, they extorted ransoms only from a small number of people with assets, but recently, the middle class has also been implicated. Therefore, those families who were able to support themselves have all moved to the urban areas or safer areas.

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

The Occurrence and Prevention of Disease (Part 1) 75

— Jin Baoshan, Technical Officer of the Department of Health

Gentlemen: The topic I am going to talk about is "The Occurrence and Prevention of Disease." Disease is the enemy of mankind and the evil of society. Therefore, we have a common saying: "Peace is a blessing, and being free from disease is like being a little immortal." However, as human reproduction increases and material civilization evolves, the causes of disease become more complex, and the chances of human health being taken away also increase. The more developed the metropolis, the more dangerous human life becomes. Because of the convenience of transportation and the same source of food and drink, all increase the chances of disease. Taking infectious diseases as an example, in the past few decades, almost every country in the world had epidemics of infectious diseases every year. Once a disease was discovered, it was like a flood or a wild beast. I don't know how many people died of disease every year, and the economic losses suffered by society due to disease were naturally very large. Therefore, if we want to seek happiness for mankind and society, we must first find a way to eliminate disease. This is very obvious. If we want to eliminate disease, we must first understand the causes of disease, and then study methods to prevent disease, and then study them. Otherwise, this "disease" will never be eradicated.

Today, let us first briefly discuss the question of "the occurrence of disease."

As human knowledge progresses, the concept of disease has gradually developed. From a historical perspective, there were legends in the Neolithic Age of drilling open skulls to release ghosts, and this is still done among the aborigines of northern Africa today. Because they believe that symptoms such as headaches and convulsions are caused by ghosts and demons in the head. Since they have no ability to understand the disease, they will naturally develop a fearful mentality and lead to superstitious ideas. In our so-called ancient civilization of China, disease and death are also believed to be in the hands of the masters in the underworld, so temples are built and monks and Taoists are followed in the hope of eradicating disease. In this way, it has been going on for thousands of years, and to this day, its remaining embers still exist, so most people still do not have a proper concept of the occurrence of disease.

It was not until the end of the eighteenth century that people gradually began to seek the causes of human disease and the location of the onset. By dissecting corpses, the discovered abnormalities were compared with the symptoms before death, and various methods were used to examine the patient's blood and excrement. Later, in the late nineteenth century, Pasteur overturned various fallacies through years of research and experience and discovered evidence of microbial disease, opening a new era in the history of medicine. As a result, human beings naturally changed their concept of disease. Only then did they realize that disease is a physiological abnormality, which is caused by our violation of the normal laws of physiology.

Modern medicine is still in its infancy, but the gloomy and dark era has passed. Although many diseases are still unclear about their origin, they have broken free from the shackles of vague metaphysics and entered the right track, and have obtained the right laws. One is to seek the truth of science through experimentation. According to modern medical knowledge, we know that there are many types of human diseases, and the causes of disease are extremely complex. These causes can be generally divided into two types. One type is called "external causes," which are caused by external effects on the body or by external invasion into the body. The other type is called "internal causes," which have been latent in the body from the beginning and are attached to body tissues. However, remember that the same cause can cause various diseases, and several causes can also jointly cause one type of disease. Now, let us explain these causes one by one, and we will naturally be able to understand the occurrence of disease.

Internal Causes: Simply put, the internal cause of disease is the human body's susceptibility to disease, so it can also be called the underlying cause of disease. Each of us has a different reaction to external stimuli. For example, a drinker can drink a lot of alcohol without getting drunk, while a person who is not used to drinking will become unconscious even if they smell alcohol. The same is true for diseases. For example, if a certain infectious disease occurs in a family, not everyone in the family will be infected and get sick. This is because there is a difference in the strength of resistance to disease, and the ease of infection is different. Resistance is medically called immunity. This immunity can generally be divided into two types: natural and acquired. Natural immunity is because of the difference in animal species, and the degree of infection with the same pathogen is different, such as the human body not being infected with cowpox. Acquired immunity is acquired after birth, such as after suffering from smallpox, the body develops immunity and can be guaranteed to never be infected again. Or use artificial methods to generate immunity, such as vaccinating with cowpox to prevent smallpox. In addition, "constitution" also has an important relationship with the occurrence of disease. Constitution is the sum of various conditions of an individual's morphology and function. If we want to have a normal life—health—we must first have a normal constitution. If the balance of life is easily lost and turns into a morbid state, that constitution is called a weak constitution—that is, it has an underlying cause of disease. The strength of the constitution is mostly directly related to our living environment and personal behavior. Whenever a part of the tissue or organ in the body has an underlying cause of disease and shows a physiological disorder, it can affect other parts, because there is a very close relationship between the various organs and systems in the body. The function of the endocrine glands is most closely related to the individual's constitution. Endocrine glands are organs that secrete certain chemical substances and directly enter the bloodstream. This substance is called a hormone, which can regulate the body's metabolism. There is also mutual connection between the various endocrine glands. Obstacles in one gland can affect other glands, so diseases caused by endocrine gland dysfunction are often very complex. "Diabetes" is an example of abnormal endocrine function. Most of these patients have an underlying cause of this disease—that is, a diabetic constitution. There have been cases in medical records of families with the disease. At the same time, it is also closely related to personal living habits. In European and American countries, the incidence of this disease is clearly increasing, which is caused by the increased amount of sugar food. There are many causes and types of diabetes, but the most common is a type caused by dysfunction of a special endocrine function in the pancreas. The occurrence of this disease can involve other organs and endocrine glands, such as the pituitary gland, thyroid gland, adrenal gland, liver, kidneys, etc. Its most obvious symptoms are thirst, easy hunger, increased urine output, and containing a large amount of sugar, the body is initially relatively obese, and then gradually becomes thin, the skin is itchy, and the starchy and sugary foods eaten are digested and absorbed into the blood, and then excreted through the urine, unable to supply the body's use. This is a result of the dysfunction of the secretory function in the pancreas, which affects the abnormal metabolism of sugars and starches. The most important thing in treatment is to pay attention to health preservation and control diet. Although there is now a special drug called "insulin" available, it is still not possible to seek a radical cure. This is a type of disease caused by the body's "internal causes." Let us now discuss the external causes of disease.

External Causes: Diseases that are caused by external stimuli are collectively called "external causes." From our daily observations, we can see that the occurrence of diseases is closely related to occupations, customs, habits, and living conditions. Climate, clothing, food, and housing also have a considerable relationship. Among them, the problem of "food" is the most important. Because the metabolism of substances and energy continues during the life of living things, and its driving force is obtained from nutrients, it goes without saying that obstacles to the supply of nutrients can endanger health and life. Nutritional disorders or deficiencies can not only directly cause disease, but also weaken the constitution and induce other diseases. In terms of physics, there are external causes of disease, such as mechanical stimuli—trauma; thermal stimuli—excessive cold or heat; air pressure, light, electric shock, etc., which can indirectly or directly cause people to become ill. In terms of chemistry, there are various poisoning situations with local and systemic effects, such as strong acids, strong alkalis, toxic gases, morphine, drugs, arsenic, phosphorus, aluminum, etc., which can directly or indirectly damage human health. In addition, the most important external causes of disease are two categories: parasites and germs. An animal that parasitizes on the body or internal organs of another animal and takes its nutrient solution for development and reproduction is called a parasite. There are many types of parasites that can cause human disease. The most common in our country are the amoeba dysenteriae that causes dysentery, the malaria protozoa, hookworms, schistosomiasis, flukes, roundworms, lung flukes, liver flukes, tapeworms, filarial worms that cause elephantiasis, etc. These parasites indirectly enter the skin through insect vectors or directly, or are excreted in feces, and then enter the digestive tract through food, directly entering the internal organs—living in the intestines, lying in the lungs, living in the liver, or swimming in the blood. They breed and reproduce, taking the human body's nutrient solution, destroying blood vessels, or other tissues, producing toxins, or blocking ducts, and causing various physiological disorders. In this way, one person spreads and infects others, harming society and the population greatly. This type of disease is collectively called "infectious diseases" because it is infectious. Among the pathogens of infectious diseases, in addition to the above-mentioned parasites, there are two types of small organisms that cannot be seen with the naked eye, called germs, and filterable viruses. Filterable viruses are extremely small and can be filtered through filters, with no form to speak of. Germs can be divided into three major categories according to their morphology, usually seen under a microscope, such as spherical ones, called cocci, rod-shaped ones called bacilli, and spiral-shaped ones called spirochetes. Each type of filterable virus or bacteria can cause a disease. Therefore, their pathogenic effects vary according to their type. Some can directly destroy tissues, and some can produce toxins. Those within the bacteria are called endotoxins, and some can produce exotoxins, which are spread throughout the body through the blood and poison body tissues. The most obvious method of infection is direct contact with the patient, which is called direct infection or contact infection. Indirect infection is caused by attachment to other objects or people and then transmission to others; some are transmitted through insect food or water media. In addition to this, there is another mode of transmission that deserves the most attention, which is the problem of carriers and shedders. A carrier appears to be healthy on the outside but does carry germs in the body and can excrete them at any time, causing others to become infected. Shedders are those who have contracted a certain infectious disease and are still shedding germs. Both of these types of people are easily overlooked, so the danger is extremely high. Now, let's give a few of the most common infectious disease examples to show the pathways of invasion into the human body: (1) Invasive through the mouth, such as cholera, dysentery, typhoid fever; (2) Invasive through the nasopharynx, such as diphtheria, scarlet fever; (3) Invasive through skin wounds, such as tetanus, erysipelas; (4) Invasive through the respiratory organs, such as pulmonary tuberculosis, pneumonia, influenza. But what we should understand is that after germs invade the human body, infectious diseases do not necessarily occur, because the occurrence of disease is a result of our body's defenses succumbing to the invading germs. Therefore, an infectious disease must follow certain "requirements" in order to occur. These requirements are: 1. The body's health disappears or decreases to a certain degree; 2. The body's immunity is weak; 3. The invasiveness of the germs is strong; 4. The toxicity of the germs has a certain strength; 5. The number of invading germs has reached the minimum required for the onset of the disease; 6. The site where the germs invade is suitable for the growth of the bacteria, so they can reproduce rapidly. For example, pulmonary tuberculosis is an infectious disease caused by the invasion of tubercle bacilli from outside the body into the human body. In our unsanitary environment, there are really many opportunities to contact these bacteria, but not every contact or all people who have contact must develop pulmonary tuberculosis, because the situation does not meet the above "requirements." This disease does not occur. Conversely, if a person is born with a tuberculosis constitution, or their health is reduced due to living against natural principles, and the body's resistance is weak, and at the same time the invasiveness of the germs is strong and the toxicity is severe, then when the number of germs gathered in the lungs increases to a considerable amount, it will immediately break out and begin to destroy the lung tissue, causing tuberculous pathological changes, poisoning the whole body, resulting in mental weakness, constant fatigue, decreased appetite, night sweats, cough, fever in the afternoon, blood in the sputum or hemoptysis, emaciation, etc. In short, all diseases, whether infectious or not, must be caused by the mutual response of the above-mentioned internal and external causes in order to produce the phenomenon of disease. This is the general outline of the occurrence of disease. As for how to prevent disease, we will continue to discuss it next time.

Datong Xing Company's Tongshun Steamer Runs Aground 84

Rescue Under Discussion

The Tongshun steamer of the Datong Xing Shipping Company in this port has a deadweight of 2,346 tons, a length of 298 feet, a width of 40 feet 3 inches, a depth of 21 feet 6 inches, and a draft of 20 feet. The steamer was built in 1896 and was built in England. Originally running between Shanghai and various ports in the north and south, the company decided to sail to Hongji to load coal and return to China. Unexpectedly, it encountered fog and had an accident on the way, and the situation was extremely dangerous.

Encountering Fog and Running Aground

According to the Datong Xing Company in Shanghai, it received a telegram from the owner of the Tongshun steamer stating that the Tongshun steamer was heading from Shanghai to Hongji and was sailing in the waters of Hainan Island when it encountered heavy fog. Navigation was difficult. At that time, the steamer mistakenly sailed onto a reef near Hainan Island in the heavy fog. The ship's hull immediately ran aground and broke the bow cabin, causing the first cabin to be flooded. The current situation is very difficult.

Emergency Telegram for Help

At that time, the shipowner was unable to move the ship's body, and the bow cabin was flooded, making it difficult to escape danger. He urgently sent a wireless telegram to report to the Shanghai headquarters, requesting rescue. After receiving the report, the company copied the original telegram to the United China Shipping Insurance Association, which insured the ship, and discussed rescue measures with Mr. Tang Danhua. It is now known that a steamer will be sent from Shanghai to Hainan Island for rescue. On the one hand, the company will first send a telegram to the owner of the Tongshun steamer to wait for rescue.

Japanese Businessmen in Shanghai's Textile Industry are Willing to Apply the Factory Law 91

On the Condition of Receiving the Same Treatment as Chinese Businesses

According to the Japanese "Mainichi Shimbun," although the National Government has not yet implemented the Factory Law since its promulgation, it is reported that it will soon be applied to factories run by foreign merchants as well. The Shanghai Japanese Textile Trade Association held a special committee meeting at the Japanese Club on the afternoon of the 7th to discuss countermeasures. All agreed that regarding the limit on the number of personnel used in factories, Japanese small and medium-sized industrialists advocate implementing it in factories with more than 50 people. On the other hand, regarding regulations on working hours, the age of child laborers, wages, and the payment of unified taxes, they are willing to accept the same regulations as Chinese businesses, but only if they are first implemented in Chinese businesses' factories. As for the unified tax, Japanese textile businesses have already paid it in full. In short, as long as there is no differential treatment compared to Chinese factories, Japanese businesses have no objections.

Chinese Medicine Community Celebrates Yesterday After the Promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations 92

More than 200 People from Over a Dozen Traditional Chinese Medicine Organizations Participated - Chairman Xia Yingtang Reported on the Process of Petitioning for the Promulgation

The Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Branch, in conjunction with various traditional Chinese medicine organizations in the city, held a supplementary celebration meeting for the promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations at the Lake Society Auditorium at 3:00 PM yesterday. More than 200 people from the traditional Chinese medicine community attended, making it a grand occasion. The details are recorded as follows:

Organizations Present

The traditional Chinese medicine organizations that attended yesterday included the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Association, the Shenzhou Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, the China Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, the Shanghai Chinese Herbal Medicine Trade Association, the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Trade Association, the Shanghai County Traditional Chinese Medicine Association, the China Medical College, the New China Medical College, the Chaozhou Heji Hospital, the Hualong Chinese Medicine Hospital, the Blue Cross Society, the Jianhua Medical Supply Company, the Medical Circle Spring and Autumn Society, the Siming Hospital, the Shanghai South Shenzhou Hospital, and more than a dozen other organizations.

Meeting Order

The entire assembly stood in solemn respect, bowing deeply to the Party and National Flag and the portrait of Dr. Sun Yat-sen; the chairman respectfully read Dr. Sun Yat-sen's last will; silence; the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting; speeches; refreshments; group photo; adjournment.

Meeting Staff

Presidium: Xia Yingtang, Director of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Branch; Ding Zhongying, Gu Weichuan, Deputy Directors; Shen Zhongfang, Chairman of the Board; Huang Peisheng, Master of Ceremonies; Cheng Dieren, Wu Quji, Recorders.

Chairman's Report

After the ceremonial procedures, Chairman Xia Yingtang first reported on the purpose of the meeting, saying, "Comrades, our branch is holding a meeting today to celebrate the promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations. I am very grateful for your participation. I would like to express my thanks, and say a few words to you. The Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations were passed by the Legislative Yuan on December 15th, 1933, and were delayed for various reasons until January 22nd of this year before being promulgated by the government. The success of a matter must involve many difficulties and cannot be achieved overnight. Our comrades have gone through much hardship in petitioning for these regulations over the past years. Even our branch has made some small contributions. Now, thanks to the government's wise decision, we can achieve our wishes. From now on, our national medicine will have a legal basis. This is truly a joyous thing. The significance of our celebration is very profound. Our branch is a government agency. Although Yingtang and others are serving in it, they are also members of the traditional Chinese medicine community. In this moment of celebration, due to the limited time, I will not say much, but I will briefly state two points that I feel, and I would like to share them with you all: Do not forget the difficulties of the past, and strive for greater progress in the future. This is just a general outline. As for the detailed methods, there are countless things to do, and it is difficult to express them all in one sentence. I hope that all comrades will contact and work together with our branch to move forward in unison. I am extremely hopeful."

Representative Speeches

After the chairman's report, Zhang Zanchen, the representative of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Association, gave a speech, saying that in order to give traditional Chinese medicine a legal status in the country, the traditional Chinese medicine community had made many efforts to petition the government to promulgate the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations. Now that these regulations have been promulgated, it is indeed something worth celebrating for our medical community. However, in the future, we should work harder to improve the academic aspects of traditional Chinese medicine, so as to raise the status of traditional Chinese medicine and enhance the belief of the general public. Gong Xingzhai, the representative of the Shenzhou Traditional Chinese Medicine Society, said that the promulgation of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Regulations is indeed something that we should celebrate enthusiastically. However, the responsibility of traditional Chinese medicine is even greater from now on. In the future, we should promote the special techniques of traditional Chinese medicine and strengthen the organization of the traditional Chinese medicine community so that the status of traditional Chinese medicine will be further consolidated. He Yunsheng and other representatives of the Traditional Chinese Medicine Society gave speeches, with similar meanings, which are omitted. After the speeches, refreshments were served, a group photo was taken, and the meeting was adjourned.

Tonnage: The "Nalaisinu" weighs 18,000 tons, is 652 feet long, 76 feet wide, and has a draft of three

The new German ship "Nalaisinu" and Captain Hunstunburg

(Photo by International News Service)

Nine feet. This ship and the "Shanghuosite" are sister ships, built by the German Weisha Factory, but its interior is equipped with steam pipes, which is slightly different from the "Shanghuosite." The average speed is 20 knots per hour, and it takes only 23 days to travel from Shanghai to Marseille.

Facilities: The ship has first-class cabins for 159 passengers and ordinary cabins for 144 passengers. The facilities are complete, the decoration is beautiful, and there are more than 110 bathrooms in the first-class cabins. Loading Capacity: The ship can also carry 11,000 tons of cargo. In addition, there are huge tanks for storing kerosene and refrigerated rooms for storing refrigerated goods. The engine is the latest type, and the cranes are controlled by electricity. The captain is Hunstunburg, who has rich sailing experience. It is scheduled to be open to the public for viewing today from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM and from 3:00 PM to 6:00 PM.

The Handling of Bills of Exchange by Silver and Money Businesses Will Continue to be Handled According to Custom 96

After Consultation Between the Money Trade Association and the Banking Association

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, after the Shanghai Foreign Exchange Banks Association abolished the custom of money shops charging banks a bill of exchange fee, the Money Trade Association believed that charging each other bill of exchange fees had become a custom, and Article 10 of the industry rules stipulated that "the minimum bill of exchange fee is one dime per thousand yuan." Therefore, the association sent commissioners Pei Yunqing and Xi Jiming to consult with Mr. Maile, manager of the McGary Bank and president of the Foreign Exchange Banks Association (i.e., the Foreign Banks Association). An agreement has now been reached to maintain the status quo and charge each other bill of exchange fees according to custom.

All City Users Oppose Telephone Charging by the Number of Calls 98

The Municipal Federation Sent a Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeking Opinions, and the District Councils Sent Letters Requesting the Convening of a Taxpayer Meeting, and Users Contributed Opinions to the Telephone Issues Committee

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the First Special District Citizens' Association of this city and the Citizens' Branch Associations of various districts, dissatisfied with the disguised price increase of the telephone company, sent letters to the Taxpayers' Association and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday to express their unanimous opinions. The details are recorded as follows:

Joint Letters of Appeal from Various District Branch Associations: The 41 district branch associations affiliated with the First Special District Citizens' Federation sent a joint letter to the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession and the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession yesterday regarding the issue of telephone price increases, urging them to convene a taxpayer meeting as soon as possible. The letter stated, "Greetings, the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department has passed a new telephone system, which will be implemented from March. This public utility matter, the Public Works Department should have obtained the consent of the city's taxpayers, but unexpectedly it is being forcibly implemented. What can be tolerated? The Public Works Department's expenses are taken from the citizens' taxes, but it disregards the suffering of the citizens and almost completely deprives them of their due rights. It is really incomprehensible. Your association is a group of taxpayers in the city, and you should uphold justice on this serious issue and convene a citywide taxpayer meeting as soon as possible for a decision. The reasons for convening a taxpayer meeting are as follows: The new telephone system is related to all citizens, but the consent of taxpayers has not been sought. The Board of Directors of the Public Works Department unilaterally advocated its passage. This should be discussed at a meeting. The market is sluggish, and it is difficult to maintain business. This is a fact. Rents have gradually decreased, which is in line with public opinion. How can prices be increased instead? Is this intended to force merchants to a dead end? This should be discussed at a meeting. Considering the above reasons, the telephone price increase issue passed by the Board of Directors of the Public Works Department is unreasonable in terms of both reason and law. Moreover, our government is implementing interest rate reductions. The official interest rate for public utilities should not exceed five percent, which is reasonable. Your association is a group of taxpayers, and it is your responsibility to not sit idly by. You should immediately convene a meeting to make a decision and live up to the expectations of the citizens. This is the end of our statement. We hope you will investigate and reply."

Letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seeking Opinions: The First Special District Citizens' Federation of this city sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce yesterday, stating, "Greetings, the Shanghai Telephone Company, in order to satisfy its desire for an annual interest rate of 10%, has formulated new charging rules and announced that they will be implemented from March 1st. In this autumn of economic depression and industrial and commercial downturn, how can we bear the additional burden? All groups in Shanghai should work together to seek a thorough resistance to relieve the citizens of unnecessary burdens. Your association is a group of merchants in the city, and you should actively seek benefits for all members to gradually eliminate the economic panic and restore the prosperity of a few years ago. Moreover, telephone use is a tool to promote commercial communication. Once restricted by per-call charges, it will be an invisible constraint, and the intangible damage to various industries will be incalculable. Our association witnessed this with a heavy heart and could not remain silent. We have specially prepared this letter, urging you to immediately notify all members, solicit opinions, and make a strong statement. Time is pressing, so please do not ignore it."

Proposing Two Opinions in Japanese Yen: The Telephone Issues Committee received a letter from Hongqiao Hospital yesterday, contributing two opinions on the issue of telephone price increases. The original text stated, "The Shanghai Telephone Company in the special district of this city has disregarded the difficulties of businesses and revised telephone rates, charging by the number of calls to increase revenue. This kind of action that only seeks private gain and disregards public convenience cannot be tolerated. All citizens should rise up and oppose it. Therefore, we contribute two methods: After the telephone company implements the new rates, all telephone subscribers should remove their telephones, so that the telephone company loses its ability to exist. After the telephone company implements the new rates, continue to use the telephones as usual, and when it is time to pay the fees, all users should stop paying at the same time. Even if they cut the lines, they cannot cut them all. Any one of these two methods, if we can unite and oppose it to the end, victory will surely belong to us. We hope that you will choose one method and quickly convene all citizens who have telephones in each branch association, verbally notify them, and inform them of the advantages and disadvantages, so that we can rise up and oppose it together to achieve our goal."

Provincial Chamber of Commerce Requests the Casting of More Copper Coins 99

The Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce Sent a Telegram to President Chiang, Forwarded to Minister of Finance Kong in Nanjing: "President Chiang of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Minister of Finance Kong, greetings: We have seen in the news that the Central Government recently ordered the mint to cast new subsidiary coins, including three types of nickel coins and two types of copper coins. The lowest value of the copper coins is half a cent. Article 3 of the newly revised Subsidiary Coin Regulations states that subsidiary coins are calculated in decimal form, with the following number of coins equal to one legal currency yuan: five 20-cent nickel coins, ten 10-cent nickel coins, twenty 5-cent nickel coins, one hundred 1-cent nickel coins, and two hundred half-cent copper coins. Article 7 states that old general-purpose subsidiary coins will be freely recalled and destroyed by the Ministry of Finance for recasting, but within the specified period, they will still be allowed to be used at market prices. The aforementioned methods and deadlines will be determined by the Ministry of Finance by order. We believe that the use of subsidiary coins is related to the social economy. The standard of living of ordinary people in China has always been very low, which cannot be compared with that of European and American countries. Therefore, even though copper coins are in general circulation, prices are still calculated in terms of 'qianwen' (cash). In recent years, due to the rising cost of living, transactions have begun to use copper coins. Ordinary people in general are already struggling to make a living. After the use of legal tender was changed last year, the prices of various commodities have actually increased by more than 20% invisibly. If subsidiary coins are used again, and the minimum value is set at half a cent, and the old subsidiary coins are clearly designated to be destroyed by the Ministry of Finance, the increase will be no less than fifteen times for those calculated in 'qianwen,' and there will also be an increase of more than half for those trading in copper coins. Prices may rise temporarily, but it is not suitable for social life. We believe that Your Excellency is well aware of the hardships of the people and is doing everything possible to help them. Unifying the legal tender is to save the financial situation, and casting subsidiary coins is to facilitate society. Therefore, on the 3rd of this month, after discussion at the executive and supervisory meeting, it was proposed that Your Excellency be requested to cast 1-li copper coins. Even if the casting of 1-li copper coins is inconvenient due to their low value, we also hope that the government will maintain the recently determined market price of 300 copper coins per legal currency yuan, and 3 copper coins per legal currency cent, and cast 2.5-li copper coins, and still maintain the nominal value calculated in 'qianwen,' to help the poor and benefit the common people. This matter concerns the circulation of subsidiary coins and affects the social economy. We dare to send this telegram on behalf of the people, respectfully requesting your review and approval. The common people will be grateful. The Jiangsu Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, bowing."

Sino-Japanese International Wireless Telephone Communication was Established at Midnight on the 14th 100

Officially Opened for Business on the 15th, Temporarily Connecting Only Beijing and Shanghai

According to Dagong News Agency, the Sino-Japanese wireless telephone service, organized by the International Wireless Telecommunications Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, has been under active preparation by both parties for several months. The communication equipment and vacuum transmission antenna have now been completely installed at the Liu Hang International Wireless Radio Station. The chief engineer has been continuously testing communication with Tokyo, Japan in recent days, and the procedures for calling and communicating are very rapid. Although the two countries are thousands of miles apart, it is as if they are talking face to face, and the sound is very clear.

Midnight Communication: The bureau and the Tokyo Radio Station in Japan have decided to open communication at 12:00 PM on the 14th of this month as the final test, and the official opening of communication is scheduled for the 15th. The communication fees for calls by officials and merchants will be collected monthly by the Shanghai Telephone Bureau in the urban area. The Shanghai Telephone Company will assist in the collection in the special district. After the end of the month, the money will be transferred to the International Wireless Radio Station. The Shanghai Telephone Company in the special district will deduct a handling fee for the service.

Connecting Beijing and Shanghai First: Because the national long-distance telephone service has not been completely completed, it has been decided that Shanghai, Nanjing, and Tokyo, Japan will communicate first, and then gradually promote it in the future. The International Wireless Telecommunications Bureau has exchanged telephone directories of Chinese rental telephones in the Shanghai area, as well as long-distance telephone directories for Nanjing and the Beijing-Shanghai-Hangzhou lines, with telephone directories of Tokyo, Japan.

Due to Snow, the Trip was Postponed

According to Shen Shi News Agency, in order to improve the safety and health facilities of local factories, the Qingdao Municipal Social Affairs Bureau organized the Qingdao City Industrial Safety and Health Observation Group to visit various factories in Beijing, Wuxi, Shanghai, and other places to observe various factory equipment and personnel management for reference. After finding a place to stay, they will rest briefly and then proceed according to the planned schedule to visit the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau and the China General Chamber of Industry and Commerce and the machine-made national goods factory. Journey to America: A Tale of Esteemed Old Students 102

A Banquet for Dr. Yung and President Li of Jiaotong University: The initial dispatch of students from our nation to study in America originated from Mr. Yung Wing's suggestion and was approved by the Qing government. Starting in the eleventh year of Tongzhi, students were sent in four batches, each consisting of thirty individuals. Mr. Yung Wing led the first batch. During the gathering, they reminisced about their time studying abroad, which they all found arduous and akin to banishment. Those without brothers were generally unwilling to go. This was contrasted with the current era, where people consider it an honor and eagerly seek opportunities to study abroad, a complete reversal of attitudes. Western Constable's Intentional Murder of Chinese: Thorough Interrogation Reveals the Truth 103

Contradictory and Disjointed Testimony: Royal Counsel Reads Report, Acknowledging Falsification of Notebook Entries

The case of Peter, the Western chief constable of the Jiaxing Road police station, and Jutte, a probationary constable, accused of intentionally murdering Chinese man Ma Debiao, has been repeatedly tried by the British Supreme Court for China. The morning's proceedings were briefly reported in yesterday's newspaper; the trial continued in the afternoon. Chief Justice Moss announced that he felt obligated to inform the jurors that when the two defendants were initially arrested, they were only charged with inflicting physical harm on Ma Debiao. Dr. Squires was summoned as a witness, testifying that on December 6 of the previous year, he examined the body of a Chinese male at the public morgue and discovered three instances of pneumonia, the earliest of which had been contracted seven or eight days prior. The judge asked, "If you were told that the person had been thrown into the river around 3 AM on December 1, what would be your assessment of the cause of death?" The response was, "I would say that being thrown into the river would have contributed to his death." The judge said, "There is no need to focus on that. Supposing that the person you saw on December 6 had been immersed in the cold water of the Hongkou River in the early morning of December 1, and was later rescued unconscious from the river and sent to the hospital, do you believe this event would have any connection to the person's death?" The response was, "Based on the results of the post-mortem examination, I would say that this event does indeed have a connection to the person's death and could account for the most recent infection of pneumonia that was discovered." Pathologist Dr. Blacklock testified that he examined some of the deceased's lung tissue under a microscope, confirming that Dr. Squire's opinion was completely accurate. Peng Lai Te, the chief constable of the Jiaxing Road police station, testified that after receiving a report from a Chinese detective, he immediately questioned the Chinese constable who drove the two defendants out that day, the constable on duty that night, Mr. Makoviskie, and a Chinese clerk to clarify everything. He then notified his superior, Mr. Gan Leidi, by telephone. Gan summoned the driver for questioning, then summoned Jutte to the office, informing him that a serious accusation had been made against him and issuing a warning. Jutte replied that everything alleged was false and asked to submit a report later. Peter was then questioned, and he also stated that the allegations were untrue and submitted a report signed by himself. An hour later, Jutte also submitted a written report. The witness could not confirm whether the two had met and discussed things, but they could have done so. (Both reports stated that they had placed Ma Debiao in the car with the intention of taking him to the police station, but halfway there, seeing that Ma was not very ill, they stopped the car and let him out.) At this point in the testimony, the court took a fifteen-minute recess for refreshments. Peng continued to testify that around noon on December 3, he received continued reports from Peter and Jutte. He cautioned the two, stating that this could be used as evidence against them in the future, intending to dissuade them from submitting the reports. However, the two insisted on submitting them. Then, with the judge's permission, the Royal Counsel read both reports in court. Although the wording differed, the main points were the same. The changes from the initial reports were that they saw Ma Debiao was very ill at the time and wanted to take Ma to the Tongren Hospital by car. When they were proceeding along Dong Hanbi Li Road, the beggar seemed to have recovered, so they decided to leave him in the Chinese area. At that time, the car was passing the Hanbi Li Road Bridge and saw two beggar boats moored across the Hongkou River, so they turned the car into Feilun Road, stopped opposite the boats, and placed the beggar on the boat, then drove back to the police station. After the reports were read, the court adjourned. At 9:45 AM yesterday, the trial resumed, and the defendant Peter spent an hour and a half testifying and defending himself. Later, at noon, he was subjected to rigorous cross-examination. The Royal Counsel asked, "Between midnight and 2 AM on December 1, you were supposed to be on duty at the Jiaxing Road police station, but you were not at the police station. What were you doing outside?" Peter stammered in reply, stating that he was lingering with a girlfriend. Peter also admitted that the words he wrote in the office notebook were fabricated, in order to protect Chief Constable Makoviskie and himself, because Ma did not report the delay of his shift truthfully. Peter also admitted that as the duty constable, he should not have left the office, but he and Jutte personally went to check on the sick beggar, which was a violation of police regulations. This was why he signed a document that he knew was not accurate. After the Royal Counsel cross-examined him thoroughly, Peter answered one by one. The Royal Counsel pointed at Peter and asked, "You once confessed that the beggar was not seriously ill and that the hospital would not accept him." This question was intended to prove that the direction in which the defendant said the car was driving was self-contradictory. The witness testimony in this case has been completed, and a verdict should be reached soon.

Xiang Yixin Kidnapping Case: Son-in-Law Initiates Crime, Sentenced 104

Xu Ruixiang, Sent to Negotiate, Was Actually the Instigator: All Six Criminals Guilty, Two Acquitted

Xiang Yixin, a native of Ningbo, owned the Xingchang Ironworks at 151 Rue Auguste Boppe. His family was quite wealthy. Xiang was a devout Buddhist and built a family temple on Gonghe Road in Zhabei, where he often went to chant sutras morning and night. In the autumn of last year, he was once kidnapped by bandits and escaped danger. However, between October 13 and January 6 of this year, he received more than ten threatening letters from the bandit gang, initially demanding 80,000 yuan, then reducing the amount to 20,000 yuan, 10,000 yuan, and finally a minimum of 5,000 yuan. Xiang sent his son-in-law, Xu Ruixiang, to negotiate with the bandits, but without success. He reported the matter to the police for arrest. Subsequently, Inspector Lu Liankui, Detective Liu Shaokui, Detectives Qian Xianting and Chen Yonggui of the General Inspectorate arrested four criminals, Gong Agen, Wei Youliang, Wang Jinzhang, and Zhang Guangen, at the Jiaotong Hotel at 37, Lane 117, Shandong Road. (It was found that this was the first batch, instigated by Xue Shandong.) It was learned that the incident was instigated by Xiang's son-in-law, Xu Ruixiang, who was an inside man. Xu lived at 52 Fanxing Lane, Xihua De Road in the Chinese area. The Sixth District Public Security Bureau sent detectives to arrest him. He confessed that his accomplice was Wang Wencheng, a native of Shandong, who lived at 31, Lane 425 of the same road, and he was also arrested. Two suspects, Liu Shanchang and Yang Fuchen, were taken into custody. Later, the First Special District Court sent a letter to transfer them, and they were sent to the Third Criminal Court along with Gong Agen and others for interrogation. Gong Agen was also found to have committed a robbery. Yang Fuchen and Liu Shanshu hired attorney Yan Gang to defend them. After deliberation and final arguments, they awaited sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefen presided over the court and sentenced Gong Agen to five years and six months of imprisonment, Xu Ruixiang to three years and six months of imprisonment, Wei Youliang, Wang Jinzhang, Zhang Guangen, and Wang Wencheng to two years each. The threatening letters were confiscated. Liu Shanshu and Yang Fuchen were acquitted and released on bail by Xu Youquan, a friend.

The proprietress of the Chen Shunbao bamboo shop, also known as "Big Sister," at No. 3 Dalin Road, West Entrance of Fangxie Back Road outside Ximen, was suddenly confronted by eight robbers around 6:30 PM last night. China Flour Mill Workers' Lawsuit: Lu Shaotang Found Not Guilty 106

When the Factory Collapsed, He Claimed He Had Already Left Shanghai; No Plaintiffs Appeared in Court

Lu Shaotang, who made a fortune by operating real estate, has suffered a significant decline in recent years due to the impact of plummeting land prices. The various businesses he operated have failed one after another. Since the closure of the Huafeng Flour Mill, where his grandfather served as general manager, the mill's workers, Jiang Kaiyang and others, sued Lu and shareholders Ye Shantao and Xu Guannan in the First Special District Court for fraud and breach of trust. At that time, Lu had left Shanghai to avoid debt, so the court temporarily suspended the portion of the case concerning Lu and summoned Ye and Xu to court for questioning. The court ruled Ye and Xu not guilty. Now that Lu has returned to Shanghai and has been arrested and detained in connection with a lawsuit against the Bank of Communications for alleged embezzlement, Judge Feng opened the court yesterday afternoon and summoned Lu to court to question him about the facts of Huafeng's closure and the fraud and breach of trust alleged by Jiang Kaiyang and others. Lu generally stated that he was unaware of the matter because he had left Shanghai when the factory collapsed. He also stated that he had heard from Ye Shantao that the workers had been dismissed with compensation. None of the workers who filed the lawsuit appeared in court. Judge Feng then announced in court that Lu Shaotang was not guilty.

Embezzlement by Employees of American Eastern Banking Corporation: White Revokes Appeal 107

Returned to McNeil Island to Serve Sentence

Leiven, the General Manager, and White, the Manager, of the American Eastern Banking Corporation, were sentenced to imprisonment by the US Court for China for alleged embezzlement and fraud. One year and five years, two years respectively. Their lawyer, Fan Keling, represented them to appeal to the court and requested bail. The request for bail was rejected by Chief Judge Hill Meek, citing legal grounds. Therefore, the two would remain in the Ward Road Prison before being escorted back to the United States. However, White has now declared his withdrawal of the appeal. Therefore, his party will be handed over to the McKinley Presidential Ship on February 18th to Seattle, then sent to McNeil Island to serve his sentence. It is expected that he will be eligible for parole when one-third of the imprisonment term has ended. As for Leiven, there has been no statement. If he continues to appeal, it remains to be determined whether he will remain imprisoned in the Ward Road Prison or be escorted to McNeil Island to await the final decision of the appellate court. A decision has not yet been made.

Silver Coin Drops, Copper Coin Rises 110

Tram Company Changes Exchange Rate

According to the Dagong News Agency, although the value of silver coins in this city has been stipulated by the Ministry of Finance to be twelve coins per legal tender yuan, the price fluctuates due to market absorption and release. Previously, due to one party hoarding a large number of silver coins, there was a sudden shortage in the market, and the price of silver coins rose sharply, with each yuan only exchanging for slightly more than eleven coins. Now, because new subsidiary coins are about to be circulated, and the credit of subsidiary coin notes is also good, fewer people in the market are collecting silver coins, so the price is falling. Yesterday, at the silver and money market, single coins were 833.3 yuan, double coins were 833.3 yuan, 1,200 coins were exchanged, and copper coins were 300,000 yuan. This morning, the exchange rate of the tram companies in the British and French concessions has also changed. The original rate of two coins for fifty copper coins, and one coin for twenty-five copper coins, has now been changed to forty-six copper coins for every two coins, and twenty-three copper coins for every one coin. As for the price of subsidiary coins, it remains at thirty copper coins for every coin.

Liu's Eulogy

Liu Haisu wrote a eulogy for Mr. Cai Zimin and his wife, Mrs. Zhou, on their double 70th birthday, saying, "The lives of the common people are mostly mediocre. If one or two individuals emerge from among them, presenting their ideas and learning, molding the people, and adapting to unprecedented changes with ease, then this singular, critical energy permeates both heaven and earth, relating to the rise and fall of the nation and its people. It is no trivial matter. Our Mr. Cai Zimin is the foremost pioneer of ideological revolution in Chinese education. During the last days of the Qing Dynasty, with internal and external troubles pressing, and the people's livelihoods in chaos, he was able to cast aside the so-called glory and reputation of the world, travel far to Europe, adopt new knowledge, and transform customs, becoming a model for later generations. After the revolution, as the first Minister of Education, he proposed the idea of aesthetic education replacing religion, instilling it in the masses. It is evident that he can expand his learning, not only perfecting himself but also working for the betterment of others. For forty years, in all kinds of weather, he has dedicated himself to transforming the customs and hearts of the world. Now, Mr. Cai is seventy years old. In the face of difficult times, he still dedicates himself to the arts and learning, hoping to save the situation and consolidate the foundation of the nation. He grasps the key points of information, and establishes high moral standards. His achievements and aspirations are truly worthy of longevity and benefit the world. Mr. Cai's virtue, reputation, and achievements are known throughout the world. His spirit is strong, just like in his prime. This is in line with Confucius's saying that the benevolent live long lives, all obtained from their nature and inherent principles, not acquired by chance. Mrs. Zhou, his virtuous spouse, is kind, respectful, frugal, knowledgeable, and learned, and is also praised by the world. Their intelligent descendants are capable of studying and saving the world, and are engaged in useful careers. After Mrs. Zhou came to be his wife, she raised several children, all of whom are intelligent. Within the family, a spirit of blessing and prosperity resides. This year, on the day and month of Mr. Cai's 70th birthday, we, his colleagues, have been inspired and guided by him, and are concerned about the decline of the nation. We dare not pick up the usual, superficial words of congratulations, and instead emphasize his virtue. We humbly express what is immortal in Mr. Cai, wishing him a strong spirit that will not weaken from seventy to old age at one hundred years old, and thus extending our national destiny to be as limitless as heaven. May Mr. Cai's thoughts and learning permeate both heaven and earth forever, and may the energy of the nation be transformed from weak to strong. This is different from the selfish prayers of the world. We respectfully write this eulogy."

Xinzha Road: Police Officer Crushed to Death by Bus 114

Brain Matter Splattered, Blood Flowing Freely

Yesterday around 6 PM, at the intersection of Xinzha Road and Chihang Bridge in the Public Concession, a uniformed police officer from the Municipal Police Bureau was riding a bicycle from west to east, speeding in front of a Route 10 bus. Upon reaching the intersection, the police officer attempted to turn south onto Chihang Road. Unexpectedly, the bicycle wheel became trapped in the tracks of a Route 3 tram, causing him to fall. A Route 10 bus, also traveling from west to east, was approaching directly behind and was unable to stop in time. The right wheel of the bus ran over the police officer's head, causing a loud crack, brain matter to splatter, and blood to flow freely. The officer on duty at the intersection witnessed the incident and recorded the bus driver's name and number. He also reported the incident to the Xinzha Police Station, which dispatched an ambulance. However, the police officer had already died. The body was transferred to Renji Hospital and then to the coroner's office for examination. The deceased was identified as Chuan Quan, ID number 1915, a 32-year-old officer from the Hengfeng Road Police Station in Zhabei, originally from Suqian. He had taken leave from the station yesterday for personal matters and was riding his bicycle when the accident occurred. Officials from the police station arrived at the scene to claim the body for burial.

North Shanghai Station: Permission Granted for Immediate Unloading of Hangzhou Fresh Produce 116

The Hangzhou City Fresh Produce and Vegetable Industry Association and the Gongchen Bridge Produce Merchants have reported that transporting fresh produce to Shanghai and only being able to unload at the South Shanghai and Maigen Road stations is too far from the market, causing delays and wilting. They requested permission to unload at North Shanghai Station. Theft at the Home of Yuan Liangbing, French Municipal Council Translator, Solved Through a Gift Certificate 119

Ding Jinxian Dared to Make Purchases, Leading to the Arrest of Multiple People

Yuan Liangbing, a translator for the French Municipal Council, residing at No. 39, Lane 93, Julida Road in the French Concession, was robbed by several armed bandits who broke into his home around 1 AM the day before yesterday. They stole clothing and cash amounting to several thousand yuan. Among the stolen items was a 50-yuan gift certificate from the Sincere Company. The number of the certificate had been recorded beforehand, and Yuan listed the stolen items and reported the theft to the French Police Station, requesting an investigation. After receiving the report, detectives Liu Jinrong and Shen Jinshu were dispatched to the gift certificate shopping department of the Sincere Company on Nanjing Road to wait. Around 2 PM that afternoon, a Shaoxing woman named Ding Jinxian (36 years old) used the stolen gift certificate from Yuan's home to make purchases at the Sincere Company. Ding was fashionably dressed and was immediately apprehended by the two detectives, along with the gift certificate, and taken back to the police station for questioning. Ding confessed that her accomplices were hiding at No. 18, Ma'an Lane, Dagu Road. Inspector Jiang Futian, investigator Wang Rusong, and detectives Yang Zhongfang, Gao Meiyan, and Weng Huanzhang, along with the Chengdu Road Police Station, dispatched Chinese and foreign detectives to the address, arresting Cao Zhibiao (20 years old, from Ningbo). Three handguns and dozens of bullets were found in the room. Cao also confessed that his accomplice, Liu Shaoshan, also known as Cao Kunshan (28 years old, from Funing), was watching a play at the Jiangbei Theater of the New Stage on Roberts Road. The detectives then went with the Sixth District Public Security Bureau to the New Stage, arresting Liu Shaoshan, also known as Cao Kunshan, his wife Liu Chen, also known as Cao Chen (21 years old), and accomplice Yun Jinlin, also known as Tang Xiaowuzi (29 years old, from the same hometown as Liu). Liu confessed that his accomplices Chen Haiqing (28 years old, from Jiangbei) and his wife Chen Cao, resided in the second-floor pavilion of No. 28, Lane 450, Yangzhou Road in eastern Shanghai. The detectives then went with the Yulin Road Police Station, dispatching a Western detective and two Chinese detectives, to secretly arrest them at the address. They first apprehended his wife Cao. Chen, hearing the police, attempted to escape by jumping out of the window, but broke his leg and fell to the ground. He was arrested and taken back to the police station, then transferred to Guangci Hospital for treatment. The arrested Yun Jinlin, also known as Tang Xiaowuzi, confessed that his accomplice Tang Xuetian was hiding on a small boat in the western section of Suzhou Creek. The detectives then went with the Sixth District Public Security Bureau to arrest Tang Xuetian. Liu Shaoshan, his wife Liu Chen, and Yun Jinlin, also known as Tang Xiaowuzi, were arrested in the Chinese Concession and are temporarily being held by the Public Security Bureau, awaiting transfer to the French Concession. Yesterday, the French Police Station sent the three suspects arrested in the French Concession, Ding Jinxian, Cao Zhibiao, and Chen Cao, to the Special Second Court, where Judge Xiong Huiping presided over the first criminal court for interrogation. Police attorney Yao Zhaodi presented the case and stated that other suspects were being held by the Public Security Bureau and requested a one-week adjournment to gather all the suspects and conduct a thorough investigation before filing charges. The investigating detectives then reported on the process of solving the case and arresting the defendants, and presented the recovered stolen items, gift certificates, and handguns and bullets to the court. When questioned, Ding Jinxian testified that her husband was involved in a lawsuit in the Chinese territory and that she had divorced him. She claimed she borrowed money from a friend yesterday to buy vegetables and was given the gift certificate, unaware that it was stolen. Cao Zhibiao's testimony was evasive. Chen Cao testified that she worked in a yarn factory and knew nothing about her husband's illegal activities. After reviewing the testimonies, the court adjourned the hearing to 9 AM on the 15th and ordered the defendants to remain in custody.

According to the Datong News Agency, the Municipal Zoo on Wenmiao Road held a domestic pigeon exhibition yesterday. A total of 152 pigeons participated. The exhibition will continue for one more day, with judging beginning this afternoon. The exhibition will close at 5 PM. Details are as follows:

Pigeon Breeds

This domestic pigeon exhibition is organized by the pigeon research association attached to the zoo. Pigeon owners registered from the 2nd to the 6th of this month. Registered pigeon owners came from more than ten locations including Shanghai, Wuxi, Yangzhou, Hangzhou, and Songjiang. Pigeon breeds included Green Shell Red Peach Blossom, Green Shell Purple Peach Blossom, Green Shell White Peach Blossom, Yellow Eye, Blood Eye, Silver White, Zijing, Dried Peach Blossom, Hybrid, and dozens of other varieties, totaling over three hundred pairs.

Exhibition Details

Yesterday was the first day of the exhibition. The zoo displayed a white banner reading "Domestic Pigeon Exhibition" at the entrance. From the entrance, small square tables were arranged in a circle, and pigeon cages were placed on them, each with a number. The cages were displayed in order. However, due to the heavy snow, pigeon owners from other locations were unable to send all their pigeons to the zoo on time, so the actual number was only 152 pairs.

Judging Today

According to a Datong News Agency reporter, among the pigeons participating in yesterday's exhibition, the Silver White, Zijing, and Dried Peach Blossom varieties were the rarest and most valuable. There was also a pair called Songjiang Gray, whose pupils were invisible to the naked eye and required lighting to be seen. This can be called a unique breed. The zoo has scheduled judging for 1 PM this afternoon. The judging criteria will be based on the pupil, feather color, and body, with points awarded to determine the winner.

Awarding Pigeon Owners

The winning pigeon owner will be presented with an inscription by a famous person, including Mayor Wu's "Soaring a Thousand Miles in One Flight," Bureau Chief Pan's "Faster Than Postal Delivery," Tong Hangbai's "Surpassing the Ordinary," Cai Jinjun's "Faster Than Mail Delivery," and over twenty others. There will also be silver cups from the Pigeon Research Association and the Municipal Zoo, as well as multiple silver shields. The judges will be pigeon experts Zhou Zhiyong, Zhang Si, Feng Yikui, He Bokang, Jiang Zuruo, and Jin Doushan. The exhibition will end tonight.
